            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report on results of a comprehensive investigation on reaction mechanisms occurring during Li uptake and release of the composite NiFe2O4/CNT.  Operando X-ray diffraction (XRD) and X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS) data collected simultaneously using one in situ cell allowed thorough elucidation of structural and electronic alterations happening during Li uptake.  From the beginning of Li uptake, the Bragg intensity of the spinel reflections decreases which can be explained by redn. of Fe3+ ions and simultaneous movement of the Fe2+ cations from tetrahedral 8a to empty octahedral 16c sites.  The redn. of Fe3+ is clearly evidenced by XAS.  The occupation of tetrahedral sites by Li+ can be excluded based on results of d. functional theory calcns.  Increasing the Li content leads to formation of a new cryst. phase resembling a monoxide with a NaCl-like structure.  The appearance of the new phase is accompanied by a steady decrease of the sizes of coherently scattering domains of the spinel and a growth of the domains of the monoxide phase.  After uptake of about 2.5 Li per NiFe2O4, all Fe3+ cations are reduced to Fe2+ and the tetrahedral 8a sites are empty (XAS spectra).  Careful Rietveld refinements of X-ray powder patterns demonstrate that the tetrahedral 8a site is successively depleted with increasing Li content.  Interestingly, the occupancy of the octahedral 16d site is also slightly reduced.  Increasing the Li content beyond 2.5 Li/NiFe2O4 leads to successive redn. of the cations to very small metal particles embedded in a Li2O matrix (as evidenced by 7Li MAS NMR investigations).  During Li release metallic Ni and Fe are reoxidized to Ni2+ resp.  Fe3+.  The cycling stability of NiFe2O4/CNT is significantly improved compared to pure NiFe2O4 or a mech. mixt. of NiFe2O4 and CNTs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrLagi4gPqvKbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgX84WExvGHrw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht1SmurvF&amp;md5=9d66e2dbf08c7241c5d885fb3ac666d2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201902485"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bresser, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Passerini, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Transition Metal Oxide Anodes for Electrochemical Energy Storage in Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Transition Metal Oxide Anodes for Electrochemical Energy Storage in Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fang, Shan; Bresser, Dominic; Passerini, Stefano</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) with outstanding energy and power d. have been extensively investigated in recent years, rendering them the most suitable energy storage technol. for application in emerging markets such as elec. vehicles and stationary storage.  More recently, sodium, one of the most abundant elements on earth, exhibiting similar physicochem. properties as lithium, has been gaining increasing attention for the development of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) in order to address the concern about Li availability and cost-esp. with regard to stationary applications for which size and vol. of the battery are of less importance.  Compared with traditional intercalation reactions, conversion reaction-based transition metal oxides (TMOs) are prospective anode materials for rechargeable batteries thanks to their low cost and high gravimetric specific capacities.  In this review, the recent progress and remaining challenges of conversion reactions for LIBs and SIBs are discussed, covering an overview about the different synthesis methods, morphol. characteristics, as well as their electrochem. performance.  Potential future research directions and a perspective toward the practical application of TMOs for electrochem. energy storage are also provided.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqAvr0rGrPgY7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgX84WExvGHrw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitFGqu7bL&amp;md5=7093cb0d8eb5176859955db6a466ecbc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1039/C7QM00175D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Progress in Conversion Reaction Metal Oxide Anodes for Li-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Mater.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent progress in conversion reaction metal oxide anodes for Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Kangzhe; Jin, Ting; Yang, Li; Jiao, Lifang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Chemistry Frontiers</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal oxides (TMOs) based on conversion reactions are attractive candidate anode materials for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) because of their high theor. capacity and safety characteristics.  In this review, we have summarized recent progress in the rational design and efficient synthesis of TMOs with controllable morphologies, compns., and micro-/nanostructures, along with their Li storage behaviors.  Single metal oxides of manganese (Mn), iron (Fe), cobalt (Co), nickel (Ni), copper (Cu), ruthenium (Ru), chromium (Cr), molybdenum (Mo), and tungsten (W) and their common binary metal oxides have been discussed in this review.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Conversion reactions for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Klein, Franziska; Jache, Birte; Bhide, Amrtha; Adelhelm, Philipp</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">38</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">15876-15887</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PPCPFQ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1463-9076</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Research on Na-ion batteries is focused on finding suitable electrode materials that enable cell reactions of high energy densities combined with low cost.  Naturally, an assessment of potential electrode materials requires a rational comparison with the analog reaction in Li-ion batteries.  The authors discuss the broad range of different conversion reactions for Na-ion batteries based on their basic thermodn. properties and compare them with their Li analogs.  Capacities, voltages, energy densities and vol. expansions are summarized to sketch out the scope for future studies in this research field.  For a given conversion electrode material, replacing Li by Na leads to a const. shift in cell potential ΔEo(Li-Na) depending on the material class.  For chlorides ΔEo(Li-Na) is nearly zero.  The theor. energy densities of conversion reactions of Na with fluorides or chlorides as pos. electrode materials typically reach values between 700 W h kg-1 and 1000 W h kg-1.  Next to the thermodn. assessment, results on several conversion reactions between Cu compds. (CuS, CuO, CuCl, CuCl2) and Na are being discussed.  Reactions with CuS and CuO were chosen because these compds. are frequently studied for conversion reactions with Li.  Chlorides are interesting because of ΔEo(Li-Na) ≈ 0 V As a result of chloride soly. in the electrolyte, the conversion process proceeds at defined potentials under rather small kinetic limitations.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpvFdD49Ctj47Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljsk3IgNFxrlg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">TiS2 as an Advanced Conversion Electrode for Sodium-Ion Batteries with Ultra-High Capacity and Long-Cycle Life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tao Hongwei; Zhou Min; Wang Ruxing; Wang Kangli; Cheng Shijie; Jiang Kai; Tao Hongwei; Wang Ruxing; Jiang Kai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1801021</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Titanium disulfide (TiS2) is investigated as an advanced conversion electrode for sodium (Na)-ion batteries (NIB) in an ether-based electrolyte (NaPF6/glyme (DME)).  The as-prepared TiS2 demonstrates a high reversible capacity of 1040 mA h g(-1) at 0.2 A g(-1) with the capacity contribution of 521 mA h g(-1) in the voltage region below 1.0 V (vs Na/Na(+)), remarkable initial coulombic efficiency of 95.9% and superior rate capability of 621 mA h g(-1) at 40 A g(-1).  The high conductivity of the Ti-based compounds and nanosized particles generated by chemical conversion reactions could minimize the entropic barrier for the reversible conversion, resulting in high reversibility and ultrafast charge/discharge ability of the electrode.  Moreover, with its strong ability to adsorb soluble polysulfide intermediates, the as-prepared TiS2 electrode exhibits superior cycling stability over 9000 cycles, serving as a stable and ultra-high capacity conversion electrode for NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQjrtMkf2pHZ6__Jf7-eMvJfW6udTcc2eYL05U2nQIx1Lntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BB3crltFCktg%253D%253D&amp;md5=48e36cf3ea11dca2481b0691679cd71c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1038/s42004-018-0084-1"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pham, D.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rod-like carbon-coated MnS derived from metal-organic frameworks as high-performance anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gao, Xiaoyan; Zhang, Xiaojie; Jiang, Jinlong; Chen, Jing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">228</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel rod-like carbon-coated MnS electrode material (MnS/C) hybrid for sodium ions batteries (SIBs) was designed by annealing Mn-based metal-org. frameworks coupled with sulfur.  When evaluated as anode material for SIBs, the typical MnS/C hybrid exhibits satisfied reversible capacity of 297 mAh/g after 100 cycles at 50 mA/g, excellent rate capability (173.9 mAh/g at 1 A/g and 143.1 mAh/g at 2.5 A/g) and robust long-term cycling stability (148.3 mAh/g after 5000 cycles at 1 A/g), showing great potential for high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpRYevCSPUhArVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljsk3IgNFxrlg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Vanadium Sulfide on Reduced Graphene Oxide Layer as a Promising Anode for Sodium Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Ruimin; Wei, Qiulong; Li, Qidong; Luo, Wen; An, Qinyou; Sheng, Jinzhi; Wang, Di; Chen, Wei; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20902-20908</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As an alternative system of rechargeable Li-ion batteries, Na-ion batteries revitalize researchers' interest due to the low cost, abundant Na resources, and similar storage mechanism to Li ion batteries.  VS4 has emerged as a promising anode material for SIBs due to low cost and its unique linear chains structure that can offer potential sites for Na storage.  Herein, the authors present the growth of VS4 on reduced graphene oxide (rGO) as SIBs anode for the 1st time.  The VS4/rGO anode exhibits promising performance in SIBs.  It delivers a reversible capacity of 362 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and a good rate performance.  The authors also study the Na storage behavior of the VS4/rGO.  Different than most transition metal sulfides, the VS4/rGO composite experiences a 3-step sepn. mechanism during the sodiation process (VS4 to metallic V and Na2S, then the electrochem. mechanism is akin to Na-S).  The VS4/rGO composite proves to be a promising material for rechargeable SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpiEKpa0_88WbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljsk3IgNFxrlg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVeqsb3K&amp;md5=1bd6b7b28b6875016174fb475c0a70f3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201901626"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zuo, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hollow Structure VS<sub>2</sub>@Reduced Graphene Oxide (RGO) Architecture for Enhanced Sodium-Ion Battery Performance</span>. <i>ChemElectroChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">78</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">85</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hollow Structure VS2@Reduced Graphene Oxide (RGO) Architecture for Enhanced Sodium-Ion Battery Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qi, Haimei; Wang, Lina; Zuo, Tiantian; Deng, Shunlan; Li, Qi; Liu, Zong-Huai; Hu, Peng; He, Xuexia</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">78-85</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHEMRA</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As a typical two-dimensional (2D) layered material, (vanadium disulfide) VS2 has huge potentials for application in SIBs due to its large interlayer spacing and high cond. compared to metal oxide or other 2D materials.  Reduced graphene oxide (RGO) possesses exceptional electronic properties and large specific area favoring fast electron transport and rich redox sites.  In this work, VS2 hollow flower spheres and RGO nanocomposites were developed for the first time, it was synthesized using a facile solvothermal method.  Benefiting from the exceptional layered structure, when used as the anode material for SIBs at room temp., the as-prepd. electrode material of VS2 hollow flower spheres @RGO (named as VS2 HFS/RGO) nanocomposites delivers a high reversible discharge specific capacity of around 430 mAh/g at c.d. of 100 mA/g, superior rate performance (2 A/g) and excellent cycling properties with the discharge capacity remained 350 mAh/g at 100 mA/g after 500 cycles.  Results show that the kinetics of VS2 HFS/RGO nanocomposites were mainly a capacitive-controlled storage process and the high capacity contribution were beneficial for good rate performance.  This work could provide new approaches and potentials for exploring and searching high performances anode materials for the practical applications of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpaMU18FO3VArVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljzXRAMFo2NLQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXit1Sms7bJ&amp;md5=06116f2d36e51b02fd25e42fefc93c80</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1021/nn406156b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">David, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bhandavat, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Singh, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoS<sub>2</sub>/Graphene Composite Paper for Sodium-Ion Battery Electrodes</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1759</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1770</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2/Graphene Composite Paper for Sodium-Ion Battery Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">David, Lamuel; Bhandavat, Romil; Singh, Gurpreet</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We study the synthesis and electrochem. and mech. performance of layered free-standing papers composed of acid-exfoliated few-layer molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) and reduced graphene oxide (rGO) flakes for use as a self-standing flexible electrode in sodium-ion batteries.  Synthesis was achieved through vacuum filtration of homogeneous dispersions consisting of varying wt. percent of acid-treated MoS2 flakes in GO in DI water, followed by thermal redn. at elevated temps.  The electrochem. performance of the crumpled composite paper (at 4 mg.cm-2) was evaluated as counter electrode against pure Na foil in a half-cell configuration.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2 Nanoflowers with Expanded Interlayers as High-Performance Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhe; Wang, Lixiu; Zhang, Kai; Wang, Jianbin; Cheng, Fangyi; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">53</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 nanoflowers with expanded interlayer spacing of the (002) plane were synthesized and used as high-performance anode in Na-ion batteries.  By controlling the cut-off voltage to the range of 0.4-3 V, an intercalation mechanism rather than a conversion reaction is taking place.  The MoS2 nanoflower electrode shows high discharge capacities of 350 mAh g-1 at 0.05 A g-1, 300 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1, and 195 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1.  An initial capacity increase with cycling is caused by peeling off MoS2 layers, which produces more active sites for Na+ storage.  The stripping of MoS2 layers occurring in charge/discharge cycling contributes to the enhanced kinetics and low energy barrier for the intercalation of Na+ ions.  The electrochem. reaction is mainly controlled by the capacitive process, which facilitates the high-rate capability.  Therefore, MoS2 nanoflowers with expanded interlayers hold promise for rechargeable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp0lywDrXEibbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljzXRAMFo2NLQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFShtL3P&amp;md5=218e207e71a96b8802293b3796174e5a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201701592"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">CuV2S4: A High Rate Capacity and Stable Anode Material for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Krengel, Markus; Hansen, Anna-Lena; Kaus, Maximilian; Indris, Sylvio; Wolff, Niklas; Kienle, Lorenz; Westfal, David; Bensch, Wolfgang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">25</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">21283-21291</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The ternary compd. CuV2S4 exhibits an excellent performance as anode material for sodium ion batteries with a high reversible capacity of 580 mAh g-1 at 0.7 A g-1 after 300 cycles.  A Coulombic efficiency of ≈99% is achieved after the third cycle.  Increase of the C-rate leads to a drop of the capacity, but a full recovery is obsd. after switching back to the initial C-rate.  In the early stages of Na uptake first Cu+ is reduced and expelled from the electrode as nanocryst. metallic Cu.  An increase of the Na content leads to a full conversion of the material with nanocryst. Cu particles and elemental V embedded in a Na2S matrix.  The formation of Na2S is evidenced by 23Na MAS NMR spectra and X-ray powder diffraction.  During the charge process the nanocryst. Cu particles are retained, but no cryst. materials are formed.  At later stages of cycling the reaction mechanism changes which is accompanied by the formation of copper(I) sulfide.  The presence of nanocryst. metallic Cu and/or Cu2S improves the elec. cond., leading to superior cycling and rate capability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoMziqiKsw51LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljzXRAMFo2NLQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXpslCks78%253D&amp;md5=f7528c5f003ac80831828dc4c6c97021</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1002/batt.201800039"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Krengel, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hansen, A.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hartmann, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">van Dinter, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bensch, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Elucidation of the Sodium – Copper Extrusion Mechanism in CuCrS<sub>2</sub>: A High Capacity, Long-Life Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Batteries Supercaps</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">176</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">183</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Elucidation of the Sodium - Copper Extrusion Mechanism in CuCrS2: A High Capacity, Long-Life Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Krengel, Markus; Hansen, Anna-Lena; Hartmann, Felix; van Dinter, Jonas; Bensch, Wolfgang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Batteries &amp; Supercaps</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The compd. CuCrS2 with a quasi-layered crystal structure was investigated as room temp. rechargeable sodium-ion battery electrode.  It exhibits excellent performance as anode material with a high reversible capacity of 424 mAh g-1 at 700 mA g-1 after 200 cycles and a capacity retention of 98.6% compared to the third cycle.  Results of ex-situ X-Ray diffraction expts. performed at different stages of the discharge process demonstrate that at the beginning of Na uptake, Cu+ cations are reduced to nanosized metallic Cu particles which are expelled from the host lattice.  Simultaneously, Na is inserted into the host material leading to the formation of Na0.7Cu0.15CrS2 with significantly expanded interlayer space.  Metallic Cu and Na0.7Cu0.15CrS2 coexist at this stage of discharge.  Increasing the amt. of Na per formula unit leads to successive conversion to X-ray amorphous Cr, nanocryst. Na2S and metallic Cu.  The formation of highly disordered metallic Cr with domain sizes in the range of few nanometers is revealed by at. pair distribution function anal.  During the charge process, the nanocryst. Cu particles are retained and Na0.7Cu0.15CrS2 is at least partially reformed.  The finely distributed Cu particles dramatically improve the long-time stability as evidenced by comparison of the electrochem. behavior of mere NaCuCrS2.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGphlHa32GMbjLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liWz9mVV6LUJg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXjsV2rtb4%253D&amp;md5=7301bcd375de136387b1ba1337df2734</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1016/j.cplett.2017.03.051"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis of Flower-like Copper Sulfides Microspheres as Electrode Materials for Sodium Secondary Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Conversion Reaction of Copper Sulfide Based Nanohybrids for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Na Rae; Choi, Jaewon; Yoon, Hyeon Ji; Lee, Min Eui; Son, Seung Uk; Jin, Hyoung-Joon; Yun, Young Soo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Sustainable Chemistry &amp; Engineering</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Intercalation-based anode materials for Na-ion batteries show relatively unfavorable electrochem. performances compared with those of Li-ion batteries because of the larger and heavier Na ion, as well as its higher electrode potential.  In contrast, conversion-reaction-based anode materials have great potential for use in Na-ion batteries.  In this study, copper sulfide nanodisks (CuS-NDs) were fabricated by a simple low-temp. reaction and applied as the anode materials for Na-ion batteries with acid-treated single-walled carbon nanotubes (a-SWCNTs), which act as a paperlike nanohybrid.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controllable Electrochemical Synthesis of Copper Sulfides as Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes with Superior Rate Capability and Ultralong Cycle Life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Haomiao; Wang, Kangli; Cheng, Shijie; Jiang, Kai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are prospective alternative to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale energy-storage applications, owing to the abundant resources of sodium.  Metal sulfides are deemed to be promising anode materials for SIBs due to their low-cost and eco-friendliness.  Herein, for the first time, series of copper sulfides (Cu2S, Cu7S4, and Cu7KS4) are controllably synthesized via a facile electrochem. route in KCl-NaCl-Na2S molten salts.  The as-prepd.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Copper sulfide nanowires/reduced graphene oxide (CuSNWs/rGO) nanocomposites are successfully synthesized via a facile one-pot and template-free soln. method in a DMSO-Et glycol (EG) mixed solvent.  It is noteworthy that the precursor plays a crucial role in the formation of the nanocomposites structure.  SEM, TEM, XRD, IR and Raman spectroscopy are used to investigate the morphol. and structural evolution of CuSNWs/rGO nanocomposites.  The as-fabricated CuSNWs/rGO nanocomposites show remarkably improved Li-storage performance, excellent cycling stability as well as high-rate capability compared with pristine CuS nanowires. The excellent lithium storage performance is ascribed to the synergistic effect between CuS nanowires and rGO nanosheets.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Uniform yolk-shell iron sulfide-carbon nanospheres for superior sodium-iron sulfide batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yun-Xiao; Yang, Jianping; Chou, Shu-Lei; Liu, Hua Kun; Zhang, Wei-xian; Zhao, Dongyuan; Dou, Shi Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-metal sulfide battery holds great promise for sustainable and cost-effective applications.  Nevertheless, achieving high capacity and cycling stability remains a great challenge.  Here, uniform yolk-shell iron sulfide-carbon nanospheres have been synthesized as cathode materials for the emerging sodium sulfide battery to achieve remarkable capacity of ∼545 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles at 0.2 C (100 mA g-1), delivering ultrahigh energy d. of ∼438 Wh kg-1.  The proven conversion reaction between sodium and iron sulfide results in high capacity but severe vol. changes.  Nanostructural design, including of nanosized iron sulfide yolks (∼170 nm) with porous carbon shells (∼30 nm) and extra void space (∼20 nm) in between, has been used to achieve excellent cycling performance without sacrificing capacity.  This sustainable sodium-iron sulfide battery is a promising candidate for stationary energy storage.  Furthermore, this spatially confined sulfuration strategy offers a general method for other yolk-shell metal sulfide-carbon composites.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrsA2QzawgLO7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4yNtnOFFIwA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhslCnt7vP&amp;md5=6002aabf08f2ca14f26ecb4cd8008b28</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.5b04700"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Douglas, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Carter, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oakes, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Share, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cohn, A.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrafine Iron Pyrite (FeS2) Nanocrystals Improve Sodium-Sulfur and Lithium-Sulfur Conversion Reactions for Efficient Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Douglas, Anna; Carter, Rachel; Oakes, Landon; Share, Keith; Cohn, Adam P.; Pint, Cary L.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11156-11165</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanocrystals with quantum-confined length scales are often considered impractical for metal-ion battery electrodes due to the dominance of solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer effects on the measured storage properties.  Here we demonstrate that ultrafine sizes (∼4.5 nm, av.) of iron pyrite, or FeS2, nanoparticles are advantageous to sustain reversible conversion reactions in sodium ion and lithium ion batteries.  This is attributed to a nanoparticle size comparable to or smaller than the diffusion length of Fe during cation exchange, yielding thermodynamically reversible nanodomains of converted Fe metal and NaxS or LixS conversion products.  This is compared to bulk-like electrode materials, where kinetic and thermodn. limitations of surface-nucleated conversion products inhibit successive conversion cycles.  Reversible capacities over 500 and 600 mAh/g for sodium and lithium storage are obsd. for ultrafine nanoparticles, with improved cycling and rate capability.  Unlike alloying or intercalation processes, where SEI effects limit the performance of ultrafine nanoparticles, our work highlights the benefit of quantum dot length-scale nanocrystal electrodes for nanoscale metal sulfide compds. that store energy through chem. conversion reactions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoQ5K7_RKr0B7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4yNtnOFFIwA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhslKlsbbL&amp;md5=04764f41c3057c65e1f434a6b7cca04a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1039/C7NR06886G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wong, K.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ng, K.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ synthesis of iron sulfide embedded porous carbon hollow spheres for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tan, Yuanzhong; Wong, Ka-Wai; Zhang, Zhiling; Ng, Ka Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>

Using this method, a porous carbon matrix and uniformly dispersed iron sulfide nanoparticles were formed simultaneously and assembled into hollow spheres.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reduced graphene oxide-wrapped FeS2 composite as anode for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Qinghong; Guo, Can; Zhu, Yuxuan; He, Jiapeng; Wang, Hongqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano-Micro Letters</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nano-Micro Letters</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Iron disulfide is considered to be a potential anode material for sodium-ion batteries due to its high theor. capacity.  However, its applications are seriously limited by the weak cond. and large vol. change, which results in low reversible capacity and poor cycling stability.  Herein, reduced graphene oxide-wrapped FeS2 (FeS2/rGO) composite was fabricated to achieve excellent electrochem. performance via a facile two-step method.  The introduction of rGO effectively improved the cond., BET surface area, and structural stability of the FeS2 active material, thus endowing it with high specific capacity, good rate capability, as well as excellent cycling stability.  Electrochem. measurements show that the FeS2/rGO composite had a high initial discharge capacity of 1263.2 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and a high discharge capacity of 344 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1, demonstrating superior rate performance.  After 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1, the discharge capacity remained at 609.5 mAh g-1, indicating the excellent cycling stability of the FeS2/rGO electrode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrjQk8sgIwCZLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4yNtnOFFIwA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXitFGrs7nK&amp;md5=8862e46f64f6b61ef3eb1b9e3b54520c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2018.07.017"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Iron Sulfide-Graphene Nanocubes Consisting of Multiple Nanoparticles with Superior Sodium Ion Storage Properties</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical iron sulfide-graphene nanocubes consisting of multiple nanoparticles with superior sodium ion storage properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiang, Juan; Liu, Zhiming; Song, Taeseup</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">283</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">683-690</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hierarchical iron sulfide nanocubes consisting of multiple iron sulfide-carbon core-shell nanoparticles coated with few-layer graphene (Fe1-xS@C/rGO) were prepd. by a two-step in-situ transformation strategy employing Prussian blue (PB) as a starting material.  The hierarchical nanocubes delivered an outstanding rate capability of 323 mAh g-1 at the c.d. of 10 Ag-1 when used as the anode of sodium ion half cells.  An iron-based sodium-ion full cell composed of a hierarchical Fe1-xS@C/rGO anode and PB cathode had a capacity of 323 mAh g-1 for 150 cycles.  We attributed the good sodium ion storage properties of the Fe1-xS@C/rGO nanocubes to the stable hierarchical building structures and the high graphitization degree of carbon obtained during the transformation process.  The graphene-coated nanocube structures inhibited the agglomeration of iron sulfide-carbon core-shell nanoparticles and accommodated the huge vol. expansion that occurred during cycling.  The high graphitization degree of carbon endowed Fe1-xS@C/rGO nanocubes with high electronic cond., facilitated sodium ion accessibility, and increased mech. durability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoZe7PGABD-_rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4yNtnOFFIwA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht1yhs77E&amp;md5=05a0117e06758289d3b1b87fbfe03d75</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1039/B703895J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bodenez, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dupont, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Laffont, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">R Armstrong, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">M Shaju, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">G Bruce, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tarascon, J.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Reaction of Lithium with CuCr<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub>—Lithium Intercalation and Copper Displacement/Extrusion</span>. <i>J. TEM, EELS and n diffraction studies provided the Cu, S and Cr oxidn. states during the 1st electrochem. step.  TEM shows the growth of Cu dendrites during the discharge of the compd. and their disappearance upon subsequent reoxidn. and EDS anal. indicates that all of the Cu cannot be extruded from the pristine phase upon discharge, nor be fully reinserted on charging.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">CuFeS2 as an anode material with an enhanced electrochemical performance for lithium-ion batteries fabricated from natural ore chalcopyrite</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Jiahui; Jiang, Feng; Li, Sijie; Xu, Zhijie; Sun, Wei; Ji, Xiaobo; Yang, Yue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Solid State Electrochemistry</span>

                        cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">CuFeS2 Quantum Dots Anchored in Carbon Frame: Superior Lithium Storage Performance and the Study of Electrochemical Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Peisheng; Song, Huawei; Liu, Yuyi; Wang, Chengxin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, a simple and quick synthetic route is reported to prep. the pure CuFeS2 quantum dots (QDs) @C composites with the unique structure of CuFeS2 QDs encapsulated in the carbon frame.  When tested as anode materials for the lithium ion battery, the CuFeS2 QDs @C composites based electrodes exhibit excellent electrochem. performances.  When charge-discharge occurred with a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1, the electrodes exhibit a high reversible capacity (760 mA h g-1) for as long as 700 cycles, which indicates the superior cycling life.  Detailed investigations of the morphol. and structural changes of CuFeS2 QDs by ex-situ XRD, ex-situ Raman, and ex-situ TEM reveal an interesting electrochem. reaction mechanism, a hybrid of a lithium-copper iron sulfide battery and lithium-sulfur battery.  The direct observation of orthorhombic FeS2 by HRTEM and the existence of Li2FeS2 detected by Raman support the assertion. such an electrochem. mechanism would attract more attention to the CuFeS2 nanomaterials as lithium ion battery anode materials.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">PVP-assisted synthesis of shape-controlled CuFeS2 nanocrystals for Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xinkai; Zhao, Yanru; Yang, Chongqing; He, Gufeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),

        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Chalcopyrite CuFeS2 with sheet-like or rod-like morphol. was synthesized by solvothermal reaction route in the presence of poly(vinylpyrrolidone) (PVP).  The concn. of PVP has significant influences on the morphol. of CuFeS2 nanocrystals.  With the increasing concns. of PVP, the sheet morphol. of CuFeS2 becomes more uniform.  Meanwhile, the av. dimensions of CuFeS2 sheets are reduced and small CuFeS2 nanoparticles are clearly decreased.  When the molar ratio of CuFeS2 to PVP is 1:2, the shape of CuFeS2 changes to rod-like, which is composed of CuFeS2 sheets.  Considering the influence of uniformity and shape of CuFeS2 nanocrystals, the CuFeS2 nanocrystals with different molar ratios of PVP have been used as active component to prep. anode for Li-ion batteries.  The Li-ion battery using CuFeS2 nanocrystals with the molar ratio of 1:2 to PVP shows the highest reversible specific capacity of ∼519 mA-h/g after 50 cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA/g and maintains a specific capacity of ∼400 mA-h/g at a d. of 1000 mA/g.  The PVP-assisted CuFeS2 electrodes are promising candidates for use as Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo8z1wbOD3uyLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj0J6zGc3R5jA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXltVans78%253D&amp;md5=9d765eef7a2ca27a686996a27e70528b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b22094"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Exploration and Size Engineering from Natural Chalcopyrite to High-Performance Electrode Materials for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exploration and Size Engineering from Natural Chalcopyrite to High-Performance Electrode Materials for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yang; Zhao, Ganggang; Lv, Xin; Tian, Ye; Yang, Li; Zou, Guoqiang; Hou, Hongshuai; Zhao, Hongbo; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6154-6165</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Compared to chemosynthetic CuFeS2, natural chalcopyrite (CuFeS2) can be regarded as a promising anode material for exploring ultrafast and stable Li-ion batteries benefiting from it being firsthand, eco-friendly, and resource-rich.  Considering the nonuniform size distribution in it and the fact that homogeneous grain distributions can effectively restrain the aggregation of active materials, the engineering of size is deemed an effective strategy to achieve excellent Li-storage performances.  Herein, varisized natural CuFeS2 are obtained by facial mineral processing technol. and outstanding Li-storage performances are exhibited.  Along with the decreasing of size, the contribution of pseudocapacitive as well as the ion transfer rates are significantly boosted.  As expected, even at 1 A g-1, a remarkable capacity of 1009.7 mA h g-1 is displayed by the sample with the smallest size and most uniform distributions even after 500 cycles.  Furthermore, supported by the detailed anal. of in situ X-ray diffraction and kinetic features, a hybrid of multiple lithium-metal sulfur systems and the major origin of the enhanced capacity upon long cycles are confirmed.  Remarkably, this work is expected to increase the far-ranging applications of natural chalcopyrite as a firsthand anode material for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and inform the readers about the effects of particle size on Li-storage performances.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqAkwoi-a1iIrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj0J6zGc3R5jA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXpvFKitw%253D%253D&amp;md5=99122fc2f39ea407104d2086db807360</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1107/S1600576717004708"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Filik, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ashton, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A software package for the calibration and processing of powder X-ray diffraction and small-angle X-ray scattering data is presented.  It provides a multitude of data processing and visualization tools as well as a command-line scripting interface for on-the-fly processing and the incorporation of complex data treatment tasks.  Customizable processing chains permit the execution of many data processing steps to convert a single image or a batch of raw two-dimensional data into meaningful data and one-dimensional diffractograms.  The processed data files contain the full data provenance of each process applied to the data.  The calibration routines can run automatically even for high energies and also for large detector tilt angles.  Some of the functionalities are highlighted by specific use cases.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr-rhX8hyW917Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljjDbV8PxAozw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXptlKntbY%253D&amp;md5=57a3801b0e76b68112d7890b24b0df89</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Juhas, P.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Farrow, C.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Crystal structure refinement of chalcopyrite, CuFeS2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hall, S.     </div><div class="casAbstract">The crystal structural of chalcopyrite, CuFeS2, were refined to an R value of 0.031 by using multiple sets of 4-circle diffractometer data and full-matrix least-squares procedures.  Spherical absorption corrections and anomalous dispersion data were applied in the refinement of the S x coordinate at site 8d (0.2574 (2), 1/4, 1/8] and the anisotropic temp. factors.  The thermal motion of all atoms is essentially isotropic and agrees, with that of equiv. atoms in cubanite, CuFe2S3.  The metal-S distances of Cu-S = 2.302 (1) and Fe-S = 2.257 (1) Å are significantly closer than those reported.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Copper oxidation state in chalcopyrite: Mixed Cu d9 and d10 characteristics</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pearce, C. I.; Pattrick, R. A. D.; Vaughan, D. J.; Henderson, C. M. B.; van der Laan, G.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Geochimica et Cosmochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2006</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">70</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4635-4642</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The detn. of the oxidn. states of copper and iron in sulfides, and chalcopyrite (CuFeS2) in particular, using 2p X-ray photoemission spectroscopy (XPS) and L2,3-edge X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS) is revisited.  Reassessment of the published spectra derived by these methods produces consistent results and reveals the 'd count' in the copper compds. to be intermediate between d9 and d10.  Nevertheless, these covalent copper compds. can be divided into those nominally monovalent and those nominally divalent.  The Fe L2,3-edge XAS of chalcopyrite, along with Moessbauer data, confirm the presence of high-spin Fe3+.  Chalcopyrite, despite recent published reports to the contrary, clearly belongs to the monovalent copper class.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRpUtljDOA8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljjDbV8PxAozw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD28XpsFyku7w%253D&amp;md5=2c2ce5c07a581bad871a0c4299f715ae</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.jmmm.2003.11.206"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Boekema, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Krupski, A.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyrite FeS2 for high-rate and long-life rechargeable sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhe; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Cheng, Fangyi; Zhang, Kai; Wang, Jianbin; Chen, Chengcheng; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1309-1316</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is desirable to develop electrode materials for advanced rechargeable batteries with low cost, long life, and high-rate capability.  Pyrite FeS2, as an easily obtained natural mineral, has been already commercialized in primary lithium batteries, but encountered problems in rechargeable batteries with carbonate-based electrolytes due to the limited cycle life caused by the conversion-type reaction (FeS2 + 4M → Fe + 2M2S (M = Li or Na)).  Herein, we demonstrate that FeS2 microspheres can be applied in room-temp. rechargeable sodium batteries with only the intercalation reaction by simultaneously selecting a compatible NaSO3CF3/diglyme electrolyte and tuning the cut-off voltage to 0.8 V.  A surprisingly high-rate capability (170 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1) and unprecedented long-term cyclability (∼90% capacity retention for 20 000 cycles) has been obtained.  We suggest that a stable elec. conductive layer-structured NaxFeS2 was formed during cycling, which enables the highly reversible sodium intercalation and deintercalation.  Moreover, 18650-type sodium batteries were constructed exhibiting a high capacity of ∼4200 mA h (corresponding to 126 W h kg-1 and 382 W h L-1) and a capacity retention of 97% after an initial 200 cycles at 4 A during charge-discharge.  This shows that the prodn. of rechargeable sodium batteries with FeS2 microspheres is viable for com. utilization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFxqeM-EGKh7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liikUocM4xcrw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1arsL0%253D&amp;md5=25c3d019d88687effcc5109727ee9bce</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.76.115413"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Masadeh, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The size-dependent structure of CdSe nanoparticles, with diams. ranging from 2 to 4 nm, was studied using the at. pair distribution function (PDF) method.  The core structure of the measured CdSe nanoparticles can be described in terms of the wurtzite at. structure with extensive stacking faults.  The d. of faults in the nanoparticles is ∼50%.  The diam. of the core region was extd. directly from the PDF data and is in good agreement with the diam. obtained from std. characterization methods, suggesting that there is little surface amorphous region.  A compressive strain was measured in the Cd-Se bond length that increases with decreasing particle size being 0.5% with respect to bulk CdSe for the 2 nm diam. particles.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyrite (FeS2) nanocrystals as inexpensive high-performance lithium-ion cathode and sodium-ion anode materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Walter, Marc; Zund, Tanja; Kovalenko, Maksym V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9158-9163</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2040-3372</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In light of the impeding depletion of fossil fuels and necessity to lower carbon dioxide emissions, economically viable high-performance batteries are urgently needed for numerous applications ranging from elec. cars to stationary large-scale electricity storage.  Due to its low raw material cost, non-toxicity and potentially high charge-storage capacity pyrite (FeS2) is a highly promising material for such next-generation batteries.  In this work we present the electrochem. performance of FeS2 nanocrystals (NCs) as lithium-ion and sodium-ion storage materials.  First, we show that nanoscopic FeS2 is a promising lithium-ion cathode material, delivering a capacity of 715 mA h g-1 and av. energy d. of 1237 Wh kg-1 for 100 cycles, twice higher than for commonly used LiCoO2 cathodes.  Then we demonstrate, for the first time, that FeS2 NCs can serve as highly reversible sodium-ion anode material with long cycling life.  As sodium-ion anode material, FeS2 NCs provide capacities above 500 mA h g-1 for 400 cycles at a current rate of 1000 mA g-1.  In all our tests and control expts., the performance of chem. synthesized nanoscale FeS2 clearly surpasses bulk FeS2 as well as large no. of other nanostructured metal sulfides.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpJgqPrpm-HGbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liikUocM4xcrw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXntFSqtLg%253D&amp;md5=642ba0e3ef151768c60da79af8485f1f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1021/ja206268a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Robert, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chernova, N.                 10.1021/ja206268a</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D133%26publication_year%3D2011%26pages%3D18828-18836%26journal%3DJ.%2BAm.%2BChem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DF.%2BWang%26author%3DR.%2BRobert%26author%3DN.%2BA.%2BChernova%26author%3DN.%2BPereira%26author%3DF.%2BOmenya%26author%3DF.%2BBadway%26author%3DX.%2BHua%26author%3DM.%2BRuotolo%26author%3DR.%2BZhang%26author%3DL.%2BWu%26author%3DV.%2BVolkov%26author%3DD.%2BSu%26author%3DB.%2BKey%26author%3DM.%2BS.%2BWhittingham%26author%3DC.%2BP.%2BGrey%26author%3DG.%2BG.%2BAmatucci%26author%3DY.%2BZhu%26author%3DJ.%2BGraetz%26title%3DConversion%2BReaction%2BMechanisms%2Bin%2BLithium%2BIon%2BBatteries%253A%2BStudy%2Bof%2Bthe%2BBinary%2BMetal%2BFluoride%2BElectrodes%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fja206268a&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c04946&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fja206268a&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Conversion Reaction Mechanisms in Lithium Ion Batteries: Study of the Binary Metal Fluoride Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Feng; Robert, Rosa; Chernova, Natasha A.; Pereira, Nathalie; Omenya, Fredrick; Badway, Fadwa; Hua, Xiao; Ruotolo, Michael; Zhang, Rui-Gang; Wu, Li-Jun; Volkov, Vyacheslav; Su, Dong; Key, Baris; Whittingham, M. Stanley; Grey, Clare P.; Amatucci, Glenn G.; Zhu, Yi-Mei; Graetz, Jason</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">133</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">46</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18828-18836</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Materials that undergo a conversion reaction with lithium (e.g., metal fluorides MF2: M = Fe, Cu, ...) often accommodate more than one Li atom per transition-metal cation, and are promising candidates for high-capacity cathodes for lithium ion batteries.  However, little is known about the mechanisms involved in the conversion process, the origins of the large polarization during electrochem. cycling, and why some materials are reversible (e.g., FeF2) while others are not (e.g., CuF2).  The authors studied the conversion reaction of binary metal fluorides, FeF2 and CuF2, using local and bulk probes to better understand the mechanisms underlying their contrasting electrochem. behavior.  X-ray pair-distribution-function and magnetization measurements were used to det. changes in short-range ordering, particle size and microstructure, while high-resoln. TEM and EELS were used to measure the at.-level structure of individual particles and map the phase distribution in the initial and fully lithiated electrodes.  Both FeF2 and CuF2 react with lithium via a direct conversion process with no intercalation step, but there are differences in the conversion process and final phase distribution.  During the reaction of Li+ with FeF2, small metallic iron nanoparticles ( &lt; 5 nm in diam.) nucleate in close proximity to the converted LiF phase, as a result of the low diffusivity of iron.  The iron nanoparticles are interconnected and form a bicontinuous network, which provides a pathway for local electron transport through the insulating LiF phase.  The massive interface formed between nanoscale solid phases provides a pathway for ionic transport during the conversion process.  These results offer the 1st exptl. evidence explaining the origins of the high lithium reversibility in FeF2.  In contrast to FeF2, no continuous Cu network was obsd. in the lithiated CuF2; rather, the converted Cu segregates to large particles (5-12 nm in diam.) during the 1st discharge, which may be partially responsible for the lack of reversibility in the CuF2 electrode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGomRjMuzUHJ2LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liNEXsd6LVeTg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXht1WksL7I&amp;md5=8b1937b1bb2422c104a24b9a0e8fa01b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1021/ic50138a009"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">DiGiuseppe, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Steger, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wold, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kostiner, E.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Preparation and Characterization of the System Copper Gallium Iron Sulfide (CuGa<sub>1-X</sub>Fe<sub>x</sub>S<sub>2</sub>)</span>. <i>Inorg.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Cu2S hollow spheres composed of nanoparticles were synthesized via a template-free hydrothermal process in the absence of additive.  The obtained Cu2S hollow spheres not only provide a large surface for contacting between electrode and the electrolyte, but also keep sufficient space for the vol. variation during the sodiation/desodiation process.  Consequently, as an anode for Na ion battery, the Cu2S hollow spheres deliver a large capacity of 369 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.2 A g-1 and demonstrated superior rate performance (331.7 mA h g-1 at 0.5 A g-1, 319 mA h g-1 at 4 A g-1) and long-term cycling stability (343 mA h g-1 at 2 A g-1 after 1000 cycles).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrrIY_cXbRNNrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liNEXsd6LVeTg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsFWhs7%252FI&amp;md5=8be649a6ee88ef8bff460bf5d3a4ca32</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b18864"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, J.</span></span>;
